# libvips Rust Port Documentation

This file was created on 2026-04-30 because `safe/PORT.md` did not exist at the start of the `impl_01_document_port` phase. It documents the current repository state, not an idealized target design.

## High-level architecture.

The port is a single Rust crate named `vips`, version `8.15.1`, defined by `safe/Cargo.toml`. It builds `cdylib`, `rlib`, and `staticlib` outputs, and `cargo metadata --manifest-path safe/Cargo.toml --format-version 1 --no-deps` reports one workspace member rooted at `safe/`; there is no Cargo workspace section in the current tree.

Directory map:
- `safe/src/abi`: C-layout structs, enums, constants, callback signatures, and ABI type declarations.
- `safe/src/runtime`: GObject-like type/object/image/region/source/target/error/memory/runtime surfaces and exported runtime functions.
- `safe/src/ops`: Operation registration, argument extraction, dispatch, generated-operation adapters, and Rust implementations for current supported operations.
- `safe/src/foreign`: Loader/saver sniffing, native JPEG/PNG/PPM/Radiance/matrix/VIPS paths, module metadata, and external process fallback handling.
- `safe/src/pixels`: In-memory image buffers, band-format conversion, interleaved pixel storage, and synchronization to/from `VipsImage`.
- `safe/src/simd`: Safe lane/vector helper code; the unsafe audit found no executable unsafe in this directory.
- `safe/src/generated`: Generated operation/deprecated compatibility metadata and registry tables.
- `safe/include/vips`: Carried public libvips-compatible headers.
- `safe/build_support`: C shim templates and compatibility C files used by Cargo/Meson builds.
- `safe/reference`: Prepared reference ABI, operation, type, pkg-config, and packaging inputs.
- `safe/tests`: Rust tests, upstream wrapper manifests, security tests, and dependent smoke harnesses.
- `safe/scripts`: Release gate, packaging, ABI/reference, introspection, and dependent-check scripts.
- `safe/debian`: Debian/Ubuntu packaging glue and package file lists.
- `safe/vendor/pyvips-3.1.1`: Vendored pyvips snapshot used by upstream/dependent validation.
- `original/libvips`, `original/cplusplus`, `original/tools`, `original/test`, `original/fuzz`: Original C/C++ snapshot and test/fuzz/tool comparison inputs.

The public boundary is the libvips-compatible C ABI/API: exported `extern "C"` and `#[no_mangle]` Rust functions, generated operation wrapper symbols, and C shim sources rendered or compiled by `safe/build.rs`. That boundary is distinct from the internal Rust data model: operation implementations generally convert or materialize `VipsImage` data into `pixels::ImageBuffer`, operate on Rust buffers and metadata, then synchronize results back into `VipsImage`/GObject-style state.

Data flow is: C callers enter through exported libvips symbols or generated operation wrappers; runtime object/type/image state stores metadata, arguments, qdata, and ownership; source/target/foreign paths load or save byte streams; operations read arguments through runtime accessors and convert images into `pixels::ImageBuffer`; outputs are written back to `VipsImage` and returned through the GObject-style runtime.

Build and packaging are layered. `safe/Cargo.toml` defines the compatibility feature surface. `safe/build.rs` generates export maps under `safe/generated/`, renders C shim sources from `safe/build_support/api_shim.c`, compiles shims with `cc`, probes `gio-2.0` through `pkg-config`, links the shim archive, and applies the `libvips.so.42` soname/version-script settings. `safe/meson.build` wraps Cargo for Ubuntu/Debian packaging, stages `libvips.so.42.17.1`, builds the C++ wrapper from `original/cplusplus`, installs headers from `build-check-install/include/vips` plus pkg-config/docs/locales/manpages from prepared reference/original material, builds tools from `original/tools`, optionally builds GIR/typelib, and builds module compatibility shared objects from original module/foreign C sources plus `safe/build_support/*_compat.c`. `safe/debian/control` and `safe/debian/rules` drive the Ubuntu 24.04 package build, upstream wrapper tests, install/reference checks, release gate, and binary package assembly.

`rg -n 'cbindgen|bindgen' safe` returned no matches. The current tree has no cbindgen or bindgen configuration; public headers are carried under `safe/include/vips` and Meson installs headers from `build-check-install/include/vips`.

## Where the unsafe Rust lives.

`rg -n '\bunsafe\b' safe --glob '*.rs'` found 3320 matches. The only non-executable match was `safe/build.rs:442`, a regex string used by `build.rs` to parse optional `unsafe extern "C" fn` declarations. The executable inventory below therefore has 3319 rows: 2988 production rows under `safe/src/**` and 331 test-only rows under `safe/tests/**`.

Grouped executable unsafe summary:
- ABI layout and callback declarations: 73 executable unsafe matches.
- Foreign loader/saver and module ABI glue: 106 executable unsafe matches.
- Internal pixel-buffer boundary: 10 executable unsafe matches.
- Operation dispatch helpers: 1443 executable unsafe matches.
- Runtime raw pointer, GLib/GObject, and libc integration: 1356 executable unsafe matches.
- Test-only C ABI harness: 331 executable unsafe matches.

The audit categories are: ABI layout and callback type declarations in `safe/src/abi/**`; public C ABI shims and GObject class/vfunc callbacks in runtime, ops, and foreign code; operation dispatch helpers that read C ABI argument state from `VipsObject` and set output fields; raw pointer access for C API/GObject structs, `GValue`, `VipsImage`, `VipsRegion`, `VipsSource`, `VipsTarget`, and GLib-owned buffers; GLib/GObject/GIO allocator/type/value/signal/quark/qdata/reference integration; libc file-descriptor and C-string integration; internal non-ABI pixel/region raw-slice and pointer conversion; and test-only C ABI harnesses. `safe/src/generated/**` and `safe/src/simd/**` have no executable unsafe matches in the current grep result.

Excluded grep false positive:
- `safe/build.rs:442` - regex string used to parse generated C ABI declarations: `Regex::new(r#"pub\s+(?:unsafe\s+)?extern\s+"C"\s+fn\s+([A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)"#)`

## Remaining unsafe FFI beyond the original ABI/API boundary.

The intended public boundary is the libvips C ABI/API implemented by exported Rust symbols and generated/C shim wrappers. The remaining FFI and non-Rust surfaces are:
- `libc` via the `libc` crate: file-descriptor syscalls and helpers such as `read`, `write`, `open`, `close`, `fstat`, `lseek`, `dup`, C strings, and POSIX types used in source/target/memory/native paths. The public ABI exposes descriptors, C strings, and GLib/C allocation conventions. Safer replacements would be `std::fs::File`, `Read`/`Write`/`Seek`, `OwnedFd`, and `CString`, but those do not by themselves preserve the C ABI surface.
- `glib-sys`, `gobject-sys`, and `gio-sys`: GLib allocation and strings, `g_malloc`/`g_free`, `g_value_*`, `g_object_*`, `g_signal_*`, `g_type_*`, quark/qdata management, boxed copy/free callbacks, object references, and GIO-compatible struct layout. The port needs these for libvips/GObject ABI compatibility. Safer gtk-rs/glib wrappers could hide some calls in a Rust-only design, but the exported ABI and layout-compatible structs still require sys-crate boundaries.
- C shim archive from `safe/build_support/api_shim.c` and generated shims rendered by `safe/build.rs`: C varargs, GValue setup, legacy/deprecated API compatibility, error/fallback wrappers, and operation wrapper shims compiled with `cc`. These preserve C calling conventions that Rust cannot express directly, especially varargs. A Rust-only API would avoid this, but it would not be ABI-compatible libvips.
- `safe/build_support/module_wrapper.c.in`: `dlopen` and `dlsym` for module initialization through GModule-compatible entry points. A Rust replacement such as `libloading` could hide dynamic loading in Rust, but the current Meson-built module ABI uses C wrappers and `G_MODULE_EXPORT`.
- Meson-built C/C++ compatibility components: C++ wrapper from `original/cplusplus`, command-line tools from `original/tools`, and original module/foreign C sources for heif, jxl, magick, openslide, and poppler modules plus compatibility C files under `safe/build_support`. These keep packaging and dependent compatibility with existing libvips consumers. Replacing them would require Rust ports of wrappers/tools/modules or narrower package scope.
- System libraries and tools linked or invoked by Meson/Debian: GLib/GObject/GIO/GModule, `dl`, libheif, libjxl/libjxl_threads, ImageMagick/MagickCore, FFTW, lcms2, OpenSlide, Cairo, and Poppler-GLib are directly used by the Meson module/tool packaging paths. Rust-native replacements would depend on format-by-format ports and would not cover all compatibility module behavior today.
- Additional Debian/control and Meson option dependencies: libjpeg, libtiff, libspng, cgif, librsvg, zlib, fontconfig/Pango/freetype, highway, matio, expat, cfitsio, libwebp, libarchive, OpenEXR, openjpeg, imagequant, doxygen, graphviz, gtk-doc, and gobject-introspection. Current Meson directly links only the subset used by enabled module builds: the GLib stack, `dl`, libheif, libjxl/libjxl_threads, MagickCore/FFTW/lcms2, OpenSlide, Cairo, and Poppler-GLib. Other items are package metadata, installed compatibility dependencies, build/doc tools, or compatibility options exposed through `safe/meson_options.txt`.
- External process fallback in `safe/src/foreign/loaders/external.rs`: `Command::new("convert")` delegates unsupported foreign loads to ImageMagick when available. This is beyond the public ABI boundary and is a user-visible fallback. A safe replacement would be native Rust loaders/savers or direct library bindings for every supported format.

Apparent FFI that is actually part of the intended boundary includes `#[no_mangle] extern "C"` libvips symbols, generated operation wrappers, GObject class/vfunc callbacks, and test declarations that link against those exported symbols. They are unsafe because they expose the original C ABI, not because they are extra hidden dependencies.

## Remaining issues.

Validation evidence from `validator-report.md` says the final clean validator matrix passed 85 cases: 5 source cases and 80 usage cases. The release gate passed, there were no approved validator-bug skips, and the report records prior fixed issues for generated-image `gravity`, JPEG materialization/load/save/thumbnail, and default truncated JPEG behavior versus strict `fail_on=truncated`. In this documentation phase, `cargo test --all-features -- --nocapture` passed from `safe/`, and `scripts/run_release_gate.sh` passed from `safe/`.

Known current unimplemented or fallback surfaces from grep:
- `safe/src/runtime/source.rs:601` - `vips_source_new_from_target` reports `not implemented`.
- `safe/src/runtime/source.rs:607` - `vips_source_new_from_options` reports `not implemented`.
- `safe/src/runtime/operation.rs:828` - `vips_operation_call_valist` reports `not implemented`.
- `safe/src/ops/mod.rs:731` - unsupported operation dispatch reports `operation not implemented`.
- `safe/build.rs:962` and `safe/build.rs:1779` - generated fallback shims report `%s is not implemented in the safe compatibility layer`.
- `safe/src/foreign/mod.rs:115` and `safe/src/foreign/mod.rs:649` - unsupported foreign input and unsupported saver errors are user-visible for formats/options outside the implemented native/module/fallback surface.
- `safe/src/runtime/image.rs:423`, `safe/src/runtime/image.rs:542`, `safe/src/runtime/header.rs:599`, and `safe/src/foreign/savers/text.rs:91` - unsupported band counts, band formats, metadata types, and matrix save formats are current error paths.

Performance status: the consulted artifacts include original libvips benchmark code and documentation, plus pyvips perf-test notes, but no benchmark result or documented performance comparison for this Rust port versus the original C/C++ libvips. This document therefore makes no performance-equivalence or performance-regression claim.

Behavioral equivalence status: the validator matrix, upstream wrappers, Rust tests, packaged reference checks, and dependent smokes are compatibility evidence, but they are not a bit-for-bit equivalence proof. The grep/evidence pass found no current supported artifact that claims bit-for-bit equivalence to original libvips and no current unresolved behavioral delta beyond the explicit unsupported/fallback surfaces above. Historical deltas in `validator-report.md` for gravity, JPEG materialization, and truncated JPEG default behavior are recorded as fixed.

Upstream coverage: `safe/tests/upstream/python-files.txt` records `baseline_passed=220, baseline_skipped=32` across 16 pytest files. The `baseline_skipped=32` value is an upstream pytest baseline note, not a declaration of current Rust-port failures. `safe/tests/upstream/manifest.json` also records Meson test wrappers, shell thumbnail tests, fuzz targets, tools, and examples.

Dependent coverage: `dependents.json` was generated for Ubuntu 24.04 amd64 and records external direct dependents plus selected ecosystem applications. `safe/tests/dependents/apps.json` has prepared smoke harnesses for nip2, photoqt, ruby-vips, pyvips, php-vips, govips, lua-vips, sharp, bimg, imgproxy, carrierwave-vips, sharp-for-go. These are smoke tests, not exhaustive dependent test suites; several use patched or generated smoke scripts and source acquisition metadata from the manifest.

CVE relevance: `relevant_cves.json` includes CVE-2018-7998, CVE-2019-6976, CVE-2021-27847, CVE-2023-40032, CVE-2026-3146, CVE-2026-3284. `safe/tests/security/*.rs` contains targeted tests for these classes: delayed-load/thread coordination, output buffer initialization, divide-by-zero/arithmetic validation, malformed text/parser handling, matrix header/input-size validation, and integer overflow/bounds validation. Safe Rust reduces many memory-corruption modes, but these CVE classes still depend on correct unsafe/FFI invariants where raw buffers, GObject ownership, file descriptors, and parser boundaries cross the ABI.

`upgrade-report.md` does not exist in the repository root in the consulted tree.

## Dependencies and other libraries used.

Direct Rust dependencies from `safe/Cargo.toml`:
- `gio-sys = "0.18"` (runtime; resolved `0.18.1`): GIO-compatible FFI type/layout surface for public ABI compatibility. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct source scan found 794 unsafe matches in generated/binding code. This is an inherently unsafe sys crate.
- `glib-sys = "0.18"` (runtime; resolved `0.18.1`): GLib allocation, strings, quarks, main/runtime primitives, and ABI layout. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct source scan found 95 unsafe matches, mostly FFI unions and binding accessors. This is an inherently unsafe sys crate.
- `gobject-sys = "0.18"` (runtime; resolved `0.18.0`): GObject type/class/property/value/signal/object-ref APIs. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct source scan found 76 unsafe matches for GObject/GValue FFI. This is an inherently unsafe sys crate.
- `jpeg-decoder = "0.3"` (runtime; resolved `0.3.2`): Native Rust JPEG header/pixel decode used by foreign loaders and JPEG materialization paths. Unsafe posture: Crate root denies unsafe_code but allows unsafe in architecture-specific SIMD/hot paths; scan found unsafe in arch SSSE3/NEON/wasm paths and decoder/idct calls. Acceptable here because it is a focused decoder dependency replacing broader C decoder exposure for native JPEG paths.
- `libc = "0.2"` (runtime; resolved `0.2.184`): C types, file descriptor syscalls, C string helpers, and allocator/syscall interop. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct source scan found many unsafe FFI declarations. This is inherently unsafe but required for fd/C ABI compatibility.
- `png = "0.17"` (runtime; resolved `0.17.16`): Native Rust PNG read/write support. Unsafe posture: Crate root has #![forbid(unsafe_code)] and direct scan found no executable unsafe beyond that marker.
- `cc = "1"` (build; resolved `1.2.59`): Compiles C shim sources rendered by build.rs. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; scan found about 20 unsafe matches in build helper internals such as OnceLock and optional jobserver/fd code. It is build-time only.
- `pkg-config = "0.3"` (build; resolved `0.3.32`): Probes gio-2.0 include/link metadata for shim compilation. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct scan found no unsafe matches. This is a narrow source inspection result, not a formal guarantee.
- `regex = "1"` (build; resolved `1.12.3`): Parses declarations and symbol inputs while generating shim/export files. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct scan found one unsafe impl in the resolved regex crate. It is build-time only.
- `serde_json = "1"` (build/dev; resolved `1.0.149`): Reads generated operation/reference JSON in build support and tests. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct scan found unsafe for unchecked UTF-8/raw-value internals. It is used for structured JSON handling in build and test code.
- `serde = "1 with derive"` (dev; resolved `1.0.228`): Derive support for test/development JSON fixtures. Unsafe posture: No forbid marker; direct scan found two unsafe matches for formatting/from_utf8_unchecked internals. It is test/development only.

Resolved versions above are from `Cargo.lock` and `cargo tree -e normal,build --prefix depth`. `serde_json` is direct in both build and dev dependency tables; it is listed once with both roles. The unsafe posture was checked with the attempted `cargo geiger --all-features` command plus direct source scans of each resolved direct dependency for `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` and `unsafe`; `cargo geiger` was unavailable in this environment.

C/C++ and system dependency surface from `safe/meson.build`, `safe/meson_options.txt`, `safe/debian/control`, and `safe/debian/rules`: GLib/GObject/GIO/GModule and `dl`; C++ wrapper/tool sources from `original/cplusplus` and `original/tools`; module libraries for heif, jpeg-xl, magick, openslide, and poppler; compatibility libraries and package metadata for libjpeg, libtiff, libspng, cgif, librsvg, zlib, fontconfig/Pango/freetype, highway, matio, expat, cfitsio, libwebp, libarchive, OpenEXR, openjpeg, imagequant, FFTW, lcms2, Cairo, doxygen, graphviz, gtk-doc, and gobject-introspection. The current Meson file links only the subset used by enabled modules and package glue; Debian metadata keeps a broader libvips-compatible dependency surface.

## How this document was produced.

The phase started by checking for an existing `safe/PORT.md` and checking `git status --short`; no `safe/PORT.md` existed. Existing dirty `.plan/**` and untracked `safe/.tmp/` state was left untouched.

Commands and files consulted:
- `test -f safe/PORT.md && sed -n '1,260p' safe/PORT.md || true`
- `git status --short`
- `find safe/src -maxdepth 3 -type f -name '*.rs' | sort`
- `find safe/include/vips -maxdepth 2 -type f | sort`
- `sed -n on safe/src/lib.rs, safe/src/abi/mod.rs, safe/src/runtime/mod.rs, safe/src/ops/mod.rs, safe/src/foreign/mod.rs, safe/src/pixels/mod.rs, and safe/src/simd/mod.rs`
- `cargo metadata --manifest-path safe/Cargo.toml --format-version 1 --no-deps`
- `cargo metadata --manifest-path safe/Cargo.toml --format-version 1`
- `(cd safe && cargo tree --manifest-path Cargo.toml -e normal,build --prefix depth)`
- `(cd safe && cargo geiger --all-features) || true; Cargo reported no `geiger` subcommand`
- `direct dependency source scans with `rg -n r"#!\[forbid\(unsafe_code\)\]|\bunsafe\b"` over each resolved direct dependency directory`
- `rg over safe/Cargo.toml and Cargo.lock for workspace, crate-type, dependency, and version evidence`
- `sed -n on safe/build.rs, safe/meson.build, safe/meson_options.txt, safe/tools/meson.build, safe/debian/control, safe/debian/rules, and safe/debian/*.install`
- `rg -n 'cbindgen|bindgen' safe || true`
- `rg -n '\bunsafe\b' safe --glob '*.rs'`
- `rg -n 'extern "C"|unsafe extern \{|no_mangle|export_name|link_name' safe/src safe/tests safe/build.rs --glob '*.rs'`
- `rg -n 'libc::|glib_sys::|gobject_sys::|gio_sys::' safe/src --glob '*.rs'`
- `rg -n 'dlopen|dlsym|G_MODULE_EXPORT|Command::new\("convert"\)|std::process::Command' safe/src safe/build_support --glob '*.rs' --glob '*.c' --glob '*.c.in'`
- `rg -n 'TODO|FIXME|todo!|unimplemented!|panic!\(|not implemented|unsupported' safe/src safe/build.rs safe/meson.build validator-report.md || true`
- `rg -n 'benchmark|bench|performance|perf|bit-for-bit|bit for bit|equivalent|mismatch|behavior|behaviour|delta|regression' safe original validator-report.md dependents.json relevant_cves.json all_cves.json || true`
- `python3 -m json.tool dependents.json`
- `python3 -m json.tool relevant_cves.json`
- `python3 -m json.tool safe/tests/upstream/manifest.json`
- `python3 -m json.tool safe/tests/dependents/apps.json`
- `sed -n '1,120p' safe/tests/upstream/python-files.txt`
- `sed -n '1,220p' validator-report.md`
- `test -f upgrade-report.md && sed -n '1,220p' upgrade-report.md || true`
- `find safe/tests -maxdepth 3 -type f | sort`
- `(cd safe && cargo build --release --all-features)`
- `nm -D --defined-only safe/target/release/libvips.so`
- `objdump -p safe/target/release/libvips.so`
- `(cd safe && cargo test --all-features -- --nocapture)`
- `(cd safe && scripts/run_release_gate.sh)`
- `git diff --check -- safe/PORT.md`

Prepared artifacts were consumed in place: `original/**`, `safe/**`, `build-check/**`, `build-check-install/**`, `dependents.json`, `relevant_cves.json`, `all_cves.json`, and `validator-report.md`. No source snapshots, CVE datasets, dependent inventories, reference manifests, validator reports, or generated ABI/header/pkg-config/test manifests were refetched or regenerated for this document.
